  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_333d6288-7745-4943-91d5-4caa48ccc67c'

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/684432-hey-guys-how-many-movies-were-made-based">hey guys how many movies were made based on that book ?? anyone knows ?? and if u do would u plz state them for me ???</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_684432'><a id="like_count_community_question_684432" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/684432?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F293101.The_Amityville_Horror">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/684432-hey-guys-how-many-movies-were-made-based">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/684432-hey-guys-how-many-movies-were-made-based">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3171366-patwell-james"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3171366-patwell-james">Patwell James</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Technically there are only two film adaptations of this book; Stuart Rosenberg's 1979 'The Amityville Horror' and Andrew Douglas' 2005 remake of the s<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Technically there are only two film adaptations of this book; Stuart Rosenberg's 1979 'The Amityville Horror' and Andrew Douglas' 2005 remake of the same name. Both are highly embellished, but the 1979 version is considerably closer to the book (the 2005 film only really resembles it in concept).<br /><br />There are many more films based on the idea of this particular house being haunted, however. In addition to the two official adaptations, there are numerous unofficial sequels and spinoffs:<br /><br />Damiano Damiani's 'Amityville II: The Possession' - 1982, based on the book 'Murder in Amityville' by Hans Holzer<br /><br />Richard Fleischer's 'Amityville 3-D' - 1983, an original screenplay<br /><br />Sandor Stern's 'Amityville: The Evil Escapes' - 1989, credited as an adaptation of the John G. Jones short story collection of the same name but in reality an original story similar in concept to the book's<br /><br />Tom Berry's 'The Amityville Curse' - 1989, based on the book of the same name by Hans Holzer; the book was set in "the" house but the movie is set in a different haunted house in Amityville<br /><br />Tony Randel's 'Amityville 1992: It's About Time' - 1992, another original screenplay in the vein of the stories from 'The Evil Escapes'<br /><br />John Murlowski's 'Amityville: A New Generation' - 1993, same as above but without crediting the book<br /><br />Steve White's 'Amityville Dollhouse' - 1996, an original screenplay<br /><br />Geoff Meed's 'The Amityville Haunting' - 2011, an original screenplay<br /><br />Andrew Jones' 'The Amityville Asylum' - 2013, an original screenplay<br /><br />Mark Polonia's 'Amityville Death House' - 2015, an original screenplay that just uses the name of the town<br /><br />John R. Walker's 'The Amityville Playhouse' (AKA 'The Amityville Theater') - 2015, an original screenplay<br /><br />And finally, Franck Khalfoun's 'Amityville: The Awakening' which is yet to be released; an original screenplay, it was filmed in 2014 but delayed multiple times for reshoots and re-edits, and is currently scheduled for release on January 6, 2017.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3412574-victoria"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1605110926i/3412574._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3412574-victoria">Victoria</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes and no. The DeFeo family was murdered by Butch DeFeo within that house. The Lutz family did move there. However, it was a hoax between the Lutz fa<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes and no. The DeFeo family was murdered by Butch DeFeo within that house. The Lutz family did move there. However, it was a hoax between the Lutz family and Butch DeFeo's lawyer to make more hype and to create waves that this book were based on. The author decided to fly with it and add some things too. Not a single thing that the book said happened in that house while the Lutz family lived there, really did happen at all. It was a good way to get publicity for sure. Both the author and the Lutz family have admitted to their stories being made up.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_6452070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6452070" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/388792-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1193146736p2/388792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6452070?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/388792-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416507697" href="/book/show/182540.The_Amityville_Horror">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/388792-jennifer?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/388792-jennifer?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/388792-jennifer?shelf=bullshit">bullshit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/388792-jennifer?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6452070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2858252524616689905">OK, folks, for the last time, here's the real story. <br/><br/>1. On 13 November 1974, a murder occurred in the home known as "High Hopes," located at what was then 112 Ocean Avenue, Amityville, New York. The victims of the crime were the DeFeo family: Ronald Sr., Louise, and four of their five children; Dawn, Allison, Mark and John. <br/><br/>2. Ronald "Butch" DeFeo, Jr., eldest son of the DeFeo family, burst into a local bar in town that night around 6:30PM, asking for help. <br/><br/>3. Butch DeFeo was later tried for and</span>
  <span id="freeText2858252524616689905" style="display:none">OK, folks, for the last time, here's the real story. <br /><br />1. On 13 November 1974, a murder occurred in the home known as "High Hopes," located at what was then 112 Ocean Avenue, Amityville, New York. The victims of the crime were the DeFeo family: Ronald Sr., Louise, and four of their five children; Dawn, Allison, Mark and John. <br /><br />2. Ronald "Butch" DeFeo, Jr., eldest son of the DeFeo family, burst into a local bar in town that night around 6:30PM, asking for help. <br /><br />3. Butch DeFeo was later tried for and found guilty of the murders of his family, and was sentenced to the Green Haven Penitentiary. Every attempt DeFeo has made to be granted parole has been rejected, he is serving consecutive life sentences. DeFeo turns 56 years old next week (09/26/07).<br /><br />4. The house was resold following the murders and probate. Among the owners since the murders were a couple named George and Kathy Lutz, who occupied the house in late 1975. The Lutzes later collaborated with an author to write this "true account" of their stay in the house. Mrs. Lutz has since passed away from cancer. <br /><br />5. No other owner of the property has complained of psychic disturbance, hauntings, paranormal activity, or any other issues with the house. The novels which followed this one claim the house is located on a Native American burial ground. No local tribe has substantiated this claim. <br /><br />6. Due to unwanted publicity, the house has been painted and the number changed to avoid onlookers. <br /><br />The murders happened, folks. They're real, they were tragic. There are some odd inconsistencies about them. But that is IT. There is NOTHING to substantiate any possession, haunting, demonology, incest, or anything else suggested in this book. It is a work of fiction, which the Lutz's lawyer later suggested they dreamed up after a night of drinking. If you want a book about a haunting, go find a good telling of the story of the Bell Witch (verified by a President of the United States) or read the "Weird" series, edited by Mark Moran. This is just nonsense. There is no basement door to hell in a quiet Long Island suburb. Sorry to disappoint everyone. <br /><br />:: steps off soapbox:: End of Rant. Thank you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2858252524616689905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416507697" href="/book/show/182540.The_Amityville_Horror">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775042055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8755850816699146007">Let's pause for a minute and laugh out loud at the fact that this stupid book was in the nonfiction section of my library. <br/><br/>HAHAHAHAHAHAHAHA<br/><br/>HAHAHA<br/><br/>HAAAAAA HAHAHA HA. HA. HAAAAAA<br/><br/>OK, I think that's good. Wait....<br/><br/>HAHAHAHAHAAAAAA OH MAN! HAHA'<br/><br/>OK...<br/><br/>That's not why it gets one lousy star anyway. It gets one star because I think it was written by a twelve year old. The writing was so bad that it distracted me from the absolutely ridiculous story. There was just no life in the story at all. I mean, the gho</span>
  <span id="freeText8755850816699146007" style="display:none">Let's pause for a minute and laugh out loud at the fact that this stupid book was in the nonfiction section of my library. <br /><br />HAHAHAHAHAHAHAHA<br /><br />HAHAHA<br /><br />HAAAAAA HAHAHA HA. HA. HAAAAAA<br /><br />OK, I think that's good. Wait....<br /><br />HAHAHAHAHAAAAAA OH MAN! HAHA'<br /><br />OK...<br /><br />That's not why it gets one lousy star anyway. It gets one star because I think it was written by a twelve year old. The writing was so bad that it distracted me from the absolutely ridiculous story. There was just no life in the story at all. I mean, the ghosts described in the book were more alive than this tired, boring (fake, yeah I said it) story. My God, man, at least use a few adjectives here and there. Give me some description of who these people are and why I should care. If this is supposed to be horrifying, why does it feel like you just learned how to write a paragraph?<br /><br />First, people moved into a house. <br />Second, weird things happened to them. <br />After that, they were scared to live there. <br />Finally, you won't believe what happened next! End of chapter cliffhanger and oh my goodness can you believe what's happening? You can't? Wow! I can't either because it didn't! And even if this was in the fiction section it wouldn't be worth your time because it feels like a story a bunch of Boy Scouts tell each other around a campfire, not something to actually read.<br /><br />That's the gist of the story with minor embellishments. Minor. <br /><br />Perhaps if someone else wrote this book, I may have cared a little more. I don't know. I don't care. <br /><br />Happy Halloween everyone! Pick a different book to scare you this year. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2303775658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2303775658" />
    <a title="Justin Tate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23082940-justin-tate"><img alt="Justin Tate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593157920p2/23082940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303775658?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Tate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Tate" href="/user/show/23082940-justin-tate">Justin Tate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303775658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12142726026144408625">Loved it. More than I should have, probably. A brilliant way to write a novel (yes, let's just admit this is a novel). The matter-of-fact, journalistic tone used to describe horrific events expertly aided the 'realism' façade, and it made for great storytelling. Toward the end the pacing went off and turned into kitchen sink horror (just throw everything out there!) but it still worked. The ending 'Afterward' was genius and is likely why this classic endures and continues to inspire a whole subg</span>
  <span id="freeText12142726026144408625" style="display:none">Loved it. More than I should have, probably. A brilliant way to write a novel (yes, let's just admit this is a novel). The matter-of-fact, journalistic tone used to describe horrific events expertly aided the 'realism' façade, and it made for great storytelling. Toward the end the pacing went off and turned into kitchen sink horror (just throw everything out there!) but it still worked. The ending 'Afterward' was genius and is likely why this classic endures and continues to inspire a whole subgenre of horror.<br /><br />If you've seen one of the zillion Amityville movies but haven't read the book, you're missing out. It's a different and wholly enjoyable experience.</span>

<div id="review_1131995166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1131995166" />
    <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile"><img alt="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606058182p2/2744708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1131995166?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile">Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1131995166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4721104815074197418">I confess, I am SO glad to be done with this book. I had to take it in just a couple chapters at a time, it just felt so overwhelmingly dark. The fact that the demons (whatever they were) didn't just throw things around the house to creep the family out, they actually affected the family members' individual personalities and seemed to truly bring out the worst in their humanity. This aspect, to me, was the most disturbing. <br/><br/>Though I never plan to read this book again and will promptly be donating</span>
  <span id="freeText4721104815074197418" style="display:none">I confess, I am SO glad to be done with this book. I had to take it in just a couple chapters at a time, it just felt so overwhelmingly dark. The fact that the demons (whatever they were) didn't just throw things around the house to creep the family out, they actually affected the family members' individual personalities and seemed to truly bring out the worst in their humanity. This aspect, to me, was the most disturbing. <br /><br />Though I never plan to read this book again and will promptly be donating my copy to my local library, I still rated it high because, as a horror book, it did its job amazingly well. It's well written and very unnerving, so despite me not actually liking it very much, it wasn't the book's fault. It was simply how it stayed in my mind. <br /><br />I did some research after finishing the book and families have proceeded to live in the home for several years at a time with no reported issues. Being that the Lutzes didn't jump on the popularity train after all this, trying to book tv show and book deals, and instead they simply disappeared to live life in peace, I can't agree with those who believe they made it all up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4721104815074197418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3564247917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3564247917" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3564247917?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23475796-the-amityville-horror">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=classic">classic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3564247917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3417874128667721436">I will start this review at the end . . . or, what I did after the end.<br/><br/>I knew some about The Amityville Horror from pop culture. I don’t think I have ever seen the movie all the way through, but I have seen parts of it. I am familiar with the house with windows like Jack O’ Lantern eyes. I knew it was a tale of possession and haunting. A story of terrors beyond imagination – terrors that only usually exist in the imagination of horror writers and filmmakers. But this really happened!<br/><br/>Or . . . did</span>
  <span id="freeText3417874128667721436" style="display:none">I will start this review at the end . . . or, what I did after the end.<br /><br />I knew some about The Amityville Horror from pop culture. I don’t think I have ever seen the movie all the way through, but I have seen parts of it. I am familiar with the house with windows like Jack O’ Lantern eyes. I knew it was a tale of possession and haunting. A story of terrors beyond imagination – terrors that only usually exist in the imagination of horror writers and filmmakers. But this really happened!<br /><br />Or . . . did it?<br /><br />When I was done, I started looking around the internet to get as much follow-up research on what really happened at 112 Ocean Avenue in Amityville, New York in the mid-1970s . . .<br /><br />Without saying too much, it seems like there is a lot of disagreement and debate about how true this story is. Sure, some of the incidents forming the foundation are 100% based in truth. But, beyond that . . . I wonder if we will ever know or society as a whole will ever agree (but, do they ever agree on anything). The book is certainly narrated as if it is all true – which lends to the creepiness and suspense . . . which is as it should be. So, if you are going in looking for non-fiction, you may leave still a bit skeptical. But, if you are just looking for a good and scary time, it should serve you well.<br /><br />All of that aside, it is a pretty entertaining and harrowing tale of demons/restless spirits who just can’t leave the people in their house alone. It is a great book if you are looking for a quick tale for a dark and chilly evening in October. I really think the only thing that could ruin it for a fan of horror and hauntings would be if you lean too much on whether it is really true or not. For me, I liked learning about the background, but when it came to enjoying it, I just let the horror of it all take me away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3417874128667721436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3873212442264240988" style="display:none">This "true" story is about as scary as a Ke$ha/Charlie Sheen lovechild. It's terrifying... but it's not the baby's fault. It was created out of a union of glitter-vomit and Tiger Blood. Mama <s>S</s>Lutz is an attention whore just in it for the money and notoriety, and Daddy is a talentless hack who just spouts random words emphatically and claims they make sense. It's like it was written by a 12 year old with ADD and then edited by someone who speaks English as a 2nd language... and started taking the classes just yesterday! Exclamation point! They have money problems and can't afford their boat or their wardrobe but never go to work. Also Officer Gionfriddo is the most badass ninja policeman! Exclamation point! He can drive down the street and totally not see that guy going into the WITCHES' BREW until <b>50 feet after he passes him</b>, and then recognize his beard, the way he walks, and the shape of his body! Crouching Gionfriddo, Hidden Ninja! Multiple Exclamation Points!! HIGH SCORE!<br><br>Father Frank had blisters on his hands. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380314570i/688954.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Then there was a lion. <br><br>Then George was all like "LET MY PEOPLE GO!" and then Gionfriddo sat quietly in his police car with the lights off watching in a non-creeper way while George acted all "like a lunatic" but later Gionfriddo said it was OK because they were closing the windows so he drove away with his lights off... totally not like a creeper, I said! <br><br>SCARY PIG! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380314570i/688955.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jodie says he's an angel but he's really a BEAST! Also, call Father Frank. <br><br>Then they moved out and then the story was over except when they levitated some more and then moved to California where levitation is illegal. <br><br>Congratulations. You've now read The Amityville Horror. <br><br>I'm sorry. </span>

<div id="review_824518129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/824518129" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/824518129?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/23517522-the-amityville-horror">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=most-excellent-audio">most-excellent-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer824518129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1184764620261323184"><br/><br/>The Amityville Horror is a book whose reviews are all over the place. On my friends list I have ratings from 1 to 5 stars all across the board. I wasn't sure where I would fall in relation to my GR buddies. <br/><br/>I listened to this one on audio as it was one of the 3 books that appealed to me and was available through OverDrive. It was a quick listen and I really enjoyed the narration. <br/><br/>I watched the movie in my teens and there have been so many of them made I really don’t know which one I watched or h</span>
  <span id="freeText1184764620261323184" style="display:none"><br /><br />The Amityville Horror is a book whose reviews are all over the place. On my friends list I have ratings from 1 to 5 stars all across the board. I wasn't sure where I would fall in relation to my GR buddies. <br /><br />I listened to this one on audio as it was one of the 3 books that appealed to me and was available through OverDrive. It was a quick listen and I really enjoyed the narration. <br /><br />I watched the movie in my teens and there have been so many of them made I really don’t know which one I watched or how good of an interpretation it was. To be honest, I don’t remember a whole lot. I remember the basement opening up to Hell and a little girl standing on the top of the roof. Other than that? Not a whole heck of a lot. <br /><br />Clearly it left a lasting impression…. ;) <br /><br />I liked the way the narrative was broken up. You get the story from a few different sources. There is the interview with the family who experienced it. There is the view of the investigator taking their statement. And there is the view of the priest that was afflicted with flu-like symptoms after trying to rid the house of evil spirits.<br /><br />It was a unique story and one that has probably been called into question since it was told. The history of the house and the mystery behind what actually happened there is part of the allure of THIS book. And I could see why others might think they made it all up.<br /><br />Sometimes there are things that are beyond explanation. There are things that cannot be explained. There are things that make us question the higher powers of the universe ; they make us question our own beliefs. <br /><br />I did enjoy the book and especially the narration. I still haven't made up my own mind as to what I believe and what I don’t. But this is a book that will resonate with me. <br /><br />The weird part of me is that reading a book like this knowing it is a real place makes me want to go buy the house and see what happens. Jeff, what do you think? Time for a change of scenery? I hear the basement down there is something forespecial!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1184764620261323184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1529673365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1529673365" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1529673365?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=horror-hazes">horror-hazes</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529673365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13727248439646029165">Actual rating 2.5/5 stars.<br/><br/>This renowned title is the supposed recounting of an actual haunting that occurred in December, 1975. The Lutz family entered their new home and resided there for just over three weeks before fleeing in terror, leaving all their possessions (pun intended) behind them.<br/><br/>Speculation is rife over whether the events depicted here were entirely fabricated by the Lutz family, highly exaggerated by Jay Anson, or an amalgamation of the two. I went into this believing it a work of</span>
  <span id="freeText13727248439646029165" style="display:none">Actual rating 2.5/5 stars.<br /><br />This renowned title is the supposed recounting of an actual haunting that occurred in December, 1975. The Lutz family entered their new home and resided there for just over three weeks before fleeing in terror, leaving all their possessions (pun intended) behind them.<br /><br />Speculation is rife over whether the events depicted here were entirely fabricated by the Lutz family, highly exaggerated by Jay Anson, or an amalgamation of the two. I went into this believing it a work of fiction and I doubt anyone but those directly involved will ever know if this is the case or not.<br /><br />My low rating stems not from the confusion around whether to classify this book as fiction or non-fiction, but in the manner the events were relayed. For a book involving the supernatural and the demonic I anticipated an abundance of chilling scenes. Instead the rather dry and direct writing style worked to dissect the haunted encounters in an analytical manner that allowed for any emotion, drama, or tension to be removed from them. This narrative style may be highly appealing to some but it unfortunately left me feeling distanced from the individuals and the supposed supernatural entities that resided alongside them in the Amityville house.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13727248439646029165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_522419352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/522419352" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/522419352?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416507697" href="/book/show/182540.The_Amityville_Horror">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=acquired-in-2013">acquired-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer522419352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18287499753503053385"><i>"Do you think it's haunted?"<br/>"No way, I don't believe in ghosts.”</i><br/><br/>It seems the reading world is clearly divided about this book. <br/>The common question obviously being: <b>is this actually true?</b> I would like to add another question to the equation: <b>does it actually matter?</b><br/><br/>To some extent, <b>it does</b>. The extent to which this novel will scare you correlates directly to (a)whether you believe the events depicted here are true and (b) your religious orientation. Personally, I’m still reserving judgement on jus</span>
  <span id="freeText18287499753503053385" style="display:none"><i>"Do you think it's haunted?"<br />"No way, I don't believe in ghosts.”</i><br /><br />It seems the reading world is clearly divided about this book. <br />The common question obviously being: <b>is this actually true?</b> I would like to add another question to the equation: <b>does it actually matter?</b><br /><br />To some extent, <b>it does</b>. The extent to which this novel will scare you correlates directly to (a)whether you believe the events depicted here are true and (b) your religious orientation. Personally, I’m still reserving judgement on just how “true” everything in here <b>may</b> or <b>may not</b> be. The spine classification says “non-fiction” but we’ve long since learnt not to believe <i>everything we read</i>. The book <b>did</b> create a storm of controversy, and I’d be very surprised if it hadn’t. It’s just that kind of book.<br /> <br />Something that did occur to me while reading this was the old adage: “Where there’s smoke…”<br /><br /><i>"I'm worried about what could happen next. Why don't you just get out of that house for a while?"</i><br /><br />Then again: take a step back and look at the book from <u>a different point of view</u>. How many <i>other</i> similar stories have you read, which you absolutely <b>knew</b> was fiction, and it still scared the living daylights out of you? It needn’t be a wasted opportunity – you have an imagination, don’t you?<br /><br />I will say this for the subject matter: if stories like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/179780.The_Exorcist" title="The Exorcist by William Peter Blatty" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exorcist</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228296.Rosemary_s_Baby" title="Rosemary's Baby by Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary's Baby</a> scared you, this book will too. Of that I don’t have <i>much</i> doubt. <b>If</b> the events depicted here <b>are</b> in fact <b>true</b>, this book’s <b>creep-factor skyrockets through the roof</b>.<br /><br /><i>”There's something in our room!"</i><br /><br />I enjoyed the book well enough. From a <u>literary point of view</u>, however, the writing is very workmanlike and matter-of-factual and, frankly, just a bit <b>bland</b>. It adds to the feeling of realism, but a few dramatic flourishes would have made the whole thing a bit more enjoyable! And let’s be honest, there <i>are</i> scenes that come across as a bit hokey. Still – it’s a fairly <b>solid three stars</b>. <br /><br /><i>”We’re trapped. It’s not going to let us go.”</i><br /><br /><u>In closing</u>. If you are one of those people who would normally skip the Foreword and Afterword of a book, it is important in the case of <i>The Amityville Horror</i> to actually read it, just to get some <u>perspective</u>. Yes, even if you think it’s hogwash. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18287499753503053385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1751677145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1751677145" />
    <a title="Robin Hill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47734324-robin-hill"><img alt="Robin Hill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475163518p2/47734324.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1751677145?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Hill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Hill" href="/user/show/47734324-robin-hill">Robin Hill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47734324-robin-hill?shelf=method-bought">method-bought</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47734324-robin-hill?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1751677145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer916132134448958479">5 stars.<br/><br/>I don’t even know where to begin. I fear this may be a long, chaotic mess of thoughts, so please bear with me, or skim, or totally ignore. <br/><br/>I’ve always been fascinated with the occult. <i>The Exorcist</i> (both the book and the movie, RIP Mr. Blatty) scared the hell out of me, pardon the pun. It still does. Every. Single. Time. And I love being scared. I love horror movies, haunted houses, Ouija boards (even though my husband forbids them), and Halloween. I love Halloween so much it’s my wedding</span>
  <span id="freeText916132134448958479" style="display:none">5 stars.<br><br>I don’t even know where to begin. I fear this may be a long, chaotic mess of thoughts, so please bear with me, or skim, or totally ignore. <br><br>I’ve always been fascinated with the occult. <i>The Exorcist</i> (both the book and the movie, RIP Mr. Blatty) scared the hell out of me, pardon the pun. It still does. Every. Single. Time. And I love being scared. I love horror movies, haunted houses, Ouija boards (even though my husband forbids them), and Halloween. I love Halloween so much it’s my wedding anniversary. <br><br>My freshman year of college, I was a moron. I had an English class where I had to write a basic research paper on anything I wanted. I chose exorcism. Why? Moron.<br><br>Fascination is one thing; belief is another. I didn’t actually <i>believe</i> all this stuff; I just liked reading about it. All my research during that semester long assignment pointed to one book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/65549.Hostage_to_the_Devil_The_Possession_and_Exorcism_of_Five_Contemporary_Americans" title="Hostage to the Devil The Possession and Exorcism of Five Contemporary Americans by Malachi Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">Hostage to the Devil: The Possession and Exorcism of Five Contemporary Americans</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/37013.Malachi_Martin" title="Malachi Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">Malachi Martin</a>. I was nineteen. This was before the internet and Amazon. I actually had to check books out of physical buildings called libraries. I had to find <i>Hostage to the Devil</i>…and I couldn’t. It had mysteriously vanished from every library within 100 miles of my college. My dad happened to find a copy in some little secondhand bookstore, and when he told the bookseller who it was for and why, the guy actually tried to convince him not to buy it. <br><br>But I’m stubborn, and my dad knew, one way or another, I'd find it. He bought it anyway. At the risk of unintentionally reviewing <i>Hostage</i> too, I’ll just say…I kind of wish he would have listened. That book messed me up. I didn’t sleep for weeks. I was on edge. Things happened in my college apartment I couldn’t explain. I managed to turn in an incomplete paper, and my professor took pity on me. He gave me a “B” and told me to get some sleep.<br><br>Why am I telling you this? I have absolutely no idea. I guess because it’s been on my mind lately, reading this book, and then yesterday with the death of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/104728.William_Peter_Blatty" title="William Peter Blatty" rel="nofollow noopener">William Peter Blatty</a> and <a> this oddly timed report </a> on Father Martin. <br><br>For at least a decade after that taxing English class, I wouldn’t go near this stuff. But time has a way of minimizing even the most frightening memories, and looking back, I’m convinced I was just sleep deprived and hormonal. <br><br><a href="http://s350.photobucket.com/user/robinhillwrites/media/Misc/IMG_20170114_132919_211_zps6nccas57.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484427194i/21717696._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_20170114_132919_211_zps6nccas57.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So here we are. I read <i>Amityville</i>, finally. Not just any <i>Amityville</i>, but a used battered paperback that looks like it holds its own demons. Was it scary? Not particularly—at least not when compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/897826.The_Exorcist" title="The Exorcist by William Peter Blatty" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exorcist</a>. Plus, to be able to read the faded print, I had the room lit up like noon in August. Was it good? Definitely. And for someone interested in the occult, it is, in fact, fascinating. If you look at the reviews, it seems the people who believe the Lutz's account rate it much higher than the people who don’t. I went into this thinking I'd be impartial; I’d just rate it as a work of fiction and leave it at that. Easier said than done, because the entire way through, I questioned everything. <i>Did this stuff really happen? If they were lying, what was their motive? How do you explain the testimony of respected corroborating witnesses like Father Mancuso and the local police force?</i> It was impossible for me to read this simply as a work of fiction, and to review it, I had to look at it from all angles. The writing, the storytelling. Fact vs. fiction. The phenomenon, the controversy, the legacy. As a whole, it's kind of brilliant.<br><br>Should you read it? If you’re into this kind of stuff? Absolutely! I wanted to go big, thus the creepy looking paperback, but if you <i>really</i> want to be scared…read the e-book version. Alone at night. With the lights out. <br><br>Oh, and sweet dreams.</span>
  <a data-text-id="916132134448958479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49845969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Nathaniel Brehmer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2135562-nathaniel-brehmer"><img alt="Nathaniel Brehmer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442615736p2/2135562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49845969?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathaniel Brehmer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathaniel Brehmer" href="/user/show/2135562-nathaniel-brehmer">Nathaniel Brehmer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49845969" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4674293429531526593">Ignore the overshadowing debate about whether or not it actually happened, and you're left with one of the most finely crafted haunted house stories ever written. The narrative is so solid, so matter-of-fact, that one cannot argue with it. This is how it happened, the book says, and what happened was horrifying. The feel is perfect, the book carries an ominous feeling from the first to the last page, much like the house on Ocean Avenue itself. Forget any of the cash-in novels or films, this is a</span>
  <span id="freeText4674293429531526593" style="display:none">Ignore the overshadowing debate about whether or not it actually happened, and you're left with one of the most finely crafted haunted house stories ever written. The narrative is so solid, so matter-of-fact, that one cannot argue with it. This is how it happened, the book says, and what happened was horrifying. The feel is perfect, the book carries an ominous feeling from the first to the last page, much like the house on Ocean Avenue itself. Forget any of the cash-in novels or films, this is a powerful, frightening masterpiece of horror. It takes a second place only to Jack Ketchum's "The Girl Next Door" as the scariest book I have ever read.</span>

<div id="review_1760044168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1760044168" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1760044168?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=halloween-bingo-2016">halloween-bingo-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1760044168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1041114307898358342"><b>Please note that I gave this book 3.5 stars, but rounded it up to 4 stars on Goodreads. </b><br/>The facts are these:<br/><br/>On November 13, 1974, Ronald DeFeo, Jr. shot and killed six members of his family at 112 Ocean Avenue, situated in a suburban neighborhood in Amityville, on the south shore of Long Island, New York. He was convicted of second-degree murder in November 1975.<br/><br/>In December 1975, George and Kathy Lutz and their three children moved into the house. After 28 days, the Lutzes left the house, claimi</span>
  <span id="freeText1041114307898358342" style="display:none"><b>Please note that I gave this book 3.5 stars, but rounded it up to 4 stars on Goodreads. </b><br />The facts are these:<br /><br />On November 13, 1974, Ronald DeFeo, Jr. shot and killed six members of his family at 112 Ocean Avenue, situated in a suburban neighborhood in Amityville, on the south shore of Long Island, New York. He was convicted of second-degree murder in November 1975.<br /><br />In December 1975, George and Kathy Lutz and their three children moved into the house. After 28 days, the Lutzes left the house, claiming to have been terrorized by paranormal phenomena while living there<br /><br />Jay Anson then wrote a book about the Lutzes experiences they had and what ultimately caused them to flee the house.<br /><br />First off, if this was a fiction book I would have given it 5 stars. Parts of the book you start to think of as too outlandish to be true (I will get to that later), but Anson takes a deft look at George and Kathy and manages to make you feel everything that they experienced. The story is broken up between these two and a priest that came to bless the house who reportedly became ill shortly after visiting, and felt as if he was being spiritually attacked by a presence from the house.<br /><br />The reason why I gave this 3.5 stars is what I found out after I finished this book. <br /><br />I did not really like George Lutz most of the book. It didn't make a lot of sense what was going on with him. I think that Anson also unwittingly revealed an angle for why the Lutzes would lie about something like this too based on a couple of things that George was upset about (IRS audit, paying a lot of money for the home, etc.). Kathy I felt detached from a lot in the book because we don't really get a sense of her until things progress further along. I had a lot of questions about her first marriage, how she met George, and her family. The two of them felt very cut off from me as a reader.<br /><br />The priest in the story didn't come off well at all (he pretty much leaves the Lutzes to their fate) and that whole aspect didn't really make a lot of sense. Plus I was curious how Anson would go and interview someone and get them to admit that they pretty much didn't care about an innocent family, he just wanted to be safe from harm. <br /><br />The writing definitely sets the mood and you keep waiting for something more terrible to happen to the Lutzes. Part of you starts to wonder if they are not just feeling things because they moved into a home where several people were murdered. <br /><br />The flow at times gets a lot choppy because a lot of things really didn't make sense here or there (the pig named Jodie) and the book at times would have an event happen but the family would ignore it.<br /><br />Anson brought in some details about the home (there are drawings included), but not much about the neighborhood or even the founding of Amitville. George Lutz makes an outrageous claim about a former owner and an Indian burial ground (isn't there always one) and it doesn't appear that Anson fact checked him at all. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Now onto why I only gave this book 3.5 stars. After I completed this I of course found out that it is more than likely (99 percent true) that the Lutzes in league with a defense attorney of Ronald DeFeo Jr. fabricated this whole story in order to make money. The Lutzes were in trouble with the IRS, they had spent too much on the home. At one point a brother in law comes over and his money is misplaced and the Lutzes heavily imply the spirits must have done it (yeah my bet is they stole it). The Lutzes went and sued a host of people (just Google) and the trial showed that the book was fiction. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am honestly wishing I had read another book for this square, oh well. I do say that since it is a classic horror novel (I read this not only for bingo, but also for my Horror 2016 book list) that is recommended to horror readers, I am glad that I finally read this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1041114307898358342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_52315111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52315111" />
    <a title="Marvin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin"><img alt="Marvin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485672728p2/2160536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52315111?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marvin" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin">Marvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52315111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8401728573943169110">This is bad in so many ways. First, it is fiction masquerading as fact. The story of this hoax is out there enough so I don't have to repeat it but the evidence should convince all but the most ardent true believer that this "true story", with the exception of the original DeFeo murder, was totally fabricated. Second, it is really terrible fiction. I am convinced that Mr. Anson had some kind of encyclopedia on hauntings and as he flipped through it he said, "Swarm of flies? I'll put that on page</span>
  <span id="freeText8401728573943169110" style="display:none">This is bad in so many ways. First, it is fiction masquerading as fact. The story of this hoax is out there enough so I don't have to repeat it but the evidence should convince all but the most ardent true believer that this "true story", with the exception of the original DeFeo murder, was totally fabricated. Second, it is really terrible fiction. I am convinced that Mr. Anson had some kind of encyclopedia on hauntings and as he flipped through it he said, "Swarm of flies? I'll put that on page twenty-two. Cold spots? page eleven." It is so sloppily put together and badly written that I'm sure Mr. Anson realized it would be no more than a bottom shelf remainder unless there was some juicy "real" paranormal tie-in. Please don't waste your time with this. There are some perfectly good books out there on paranormal sightings and lots of great haunted house novels like Shirley Jackson's <i>The Haunting of Hill House</i> or Richard Matheson's <i>Hell HousE</i> that will thrill you. And just for the record, all of those Amityville movies suck too. Don't ask me why I bothered to watch them after hating the book so much. I guess I'm a masochist.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2799965361" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2799965361" />
    <a title="Cameron Chaney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40648249-cameron-chaney"><img alt="Cameron Chaney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596633386p2/40648249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2799965361?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cameron Chaney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cameron Chaney" href="/user/show/40648249-cameron-chaney">Cameron Chaney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40648249-cameron-chaney?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2799965361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1557602597738871315">Now that I have seen <i>The Amityville Horror</i> film (1979), watched numerous documentaries on the house, and read the book, I can safely say that the best "adaptation" of the Amityville story will always be <i>My Amityville Horror</i> (2013). This is a documentary following one of the Lutz children - now an adult - and shows what the he remembers from his time at 112 Ocean Ave in Amityville, NY. What we get is not exactly what one would expect from a documentary about the Amityville house. Instead, it is a</span>
  <span id="freeText1557602597738871315" style="display:none">Now that I have seen <i>The Amityville Horror</i> film (1979), watched numerous documentaries on the house, and read the book, I can safely say that the best "adaptation" of the Amityville story will always be <i>My Amityville Horror</i> (2013). This is a documentary following one of the Lutz children - now an adult - and shows what the he remembers from his time at 112 Ocean Ave in Amityville, NY. What we get is not exactly what one would expect from a documentary about the Amityville house. Instead, it is a deep psychological study about an attention-hungry family hellbent on making a mark for themselves by exploiting their "haunted" home and the tragic events that occurred there.<br /><br />Was the house actually haunted? The Lutz child believes so, even to this day. But he is also a man with mental damage and intense anger issues, one who believes his abusive stepfather was an evil man who practiced witchcraft to provoke the Amityville spirits. This adds a whole new layer of mystery and fascination onto the Amityville happening, showing that there might be more to the story than what meets the eye.<br /><br />Unfortunately, <i>The Amityville Horror</i> by Jay Anson is nowhere near as intriguing. What we get is a dry account of what George and Kathleen Lutz claim to have happened during their time living in this house. It's your standard haunted house story; a happy American family moves into their dream-home, but when creepy shit starts happening, they discover that their dream-home isn't so dreamy after all.<br /><br />Of course, George and Kathleen Lutz are not portrayed as being the money-hungry, abusive, manipulative people that their son later described them as being in <i>My Amityville Horror</i>, nor is George a practitioner of the dark arts. Instead, they are described as being an average married couple, doing whatever they can to keep their children safe.<br /><br />Listen, while I do believe in ghosts, I don't know what's true and what isn't about this story. There are so many conflicting testimonies and details. For example, at the end of this book, Anson says that after the Lutz family moved out of 112 Ocean Avenue, Kathleen Lutz never spoke of the events again. This is bullshit. Anson said only a few pages prior that Kathleen gave a detailed re-accounting of her story in preparation of this book. Also, Mr. and Mrs. Lutz appeared on TV on multiple occasions to promote their story and it's many adaptations. They made a helluva lot of bank by being in the spotlight. Neither of them retreated into the shadows, hiding from whatever forces haunted them at the Amityville house. They definitely exploited their story, and what's not to say they didn't exaggerate the details, twist the truth, or flat-out lie about the whole thing?<br /><br />Honestly, this is what makes <i>The Amityville Horror</i> so interesting. While the book itself is dry and not very scary (minus the pig-thing, which is quite terrifying), there are so many conflicting stories that keep me intrigued in the Lutz family and what really went on behind those closed doors. I guess we'll never know for sure, but one thing is for certain; the Lutz family certainly made their mark in our culture, whether they were trying to or not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1557602597738871315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_400592398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400592398" />
    <a title="Mindi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6157592-mindi"><img alt="Mindi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538422738p2/6157592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400592398?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mindi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mindi" href="/user/show/6157592-mindi">Mindi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416507697" href="/book/show/182540.The_Amityville_Horror">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400592398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3041285939282409824">About 15 years ago I picked up a copy of this book and had to put it down indefinitely. It was slowly creeping me out, and when I got to the part where George Lutz sees a creepy pig behind his daughter in her bedroom window in the middle of the night I said "nope". However, I kept the book, because I knew one day I would finish it. Yesterday was that day, and I really wish I hadn't bothered.<br/><br/>I was in my twenties the first time I tried to read this, and although I was reading a lot of horror, for </span>
  <span id="freeText3041285939282409824" style="display:none">About 15 years ago I picked up a copy of this book and had to put it down indefinitely. It was slowly creeping me out, and when I got to the part where George Lutz sees a creepy pig behind his daughter in her bedroom window in the middle of the night I said "nope". However, I kept the book, because I knew one day I would finish it. Yesterday was that day, and I really wish I hadn't bothered.<br /><br />I was in my twenties the first time I tried to read this, and although I was reading a lot of horror, for some reason this one got to me. It takes place the year I was born, and was written in 1977. I'm going to say right now that I don't believe these things actually happened to the Lutz family. I'm super skeptical, I always have been, and anytime something paranormal says "based on a true story" I know that writers are just trying to sensationalize a story. People love those tag lines. The fact that something so heinous could actually happen to people in real life is something that readers eat up. I take it with a grain of salt. <br /><br />Should I address my problems with the writing first, or the story? Let's start with the writing.<br /><br />Anson has this incredibly annoying habit of ending every dramatic sentence with an exclamation point. I'm sure people have been talking about this one since the book was released, but it's really unnecessary, and it actually takes a statement that could be rather chilling with just a simple period at the end and it makes it sound ridiculous. It's like when people use all caps and it sounds like they're screaming. Every time Anson used an exclamation point, I imaged him wide eyed, and gasping at the horror of the event he had just described. It diffuses all the tension, and by the end of the book it's comical. <br /><br />Now, let's discuss the story. The Lutz family moves into 112 Ocean Avenue on December 18, 1975. On November 13, 1974, 23-year-old Ronald DeFeo shot and killed his parents and 4 siblings as they slept in the house at 112 Ocean Avenue. The Lutzes know the house is the site of multiple murders, but they aren't superstitious, so they dismiss any worries over living in a house where violent murders occurred, and actually end up buying a number of pieces of furniture and appliances that were left behind after there was nobody alive to claim them. Which to me is gross and morbid, but whatever.<br /><br />Practically from the moment they step into the house things get weird. I started reading this again at night, and the strange occurrences were actually still kinda creepy 15 years later. Things start small, so I can understand the Lutzes not feeling the need to flee in terror right away. George is constantly freezing, and spends hours feeding logs into the living room fireplace. He also wakes up every night at 3:15 on the dot and has a compulsion to check the boat house behind the home. Kathleen smells perfume in odd places, especially in the kitchen, where she begins to feel a "presence". Both parents are also quick to lose their tempers, and feel that their 3 children are acting out more. They were never easily angered before moving into the house. At this point, I'm invested. Things are quietly creepy, and when one night George goes out to the boat house and turns around to see his 5-year-old daughter standing in the window with a pig behind her, the creepy goes up a notch. <br /><br />Sadly, and I'm sure there wouldn't be a book if this never happened, the crazy things that are happening in the house begin to escalate beyond what anyone would actually stay and allow to happen, and yet the Lutz family does stay, and bad things continue to befall them. A local priest even tells them to leave the house, and they don't listen to him. It's infuriating. Both George and Kathleen know that something is horribly wrong in their house, but they continue to try to ignore it, and put their own lives and the lives of their children in danger. The front door is inexplicably torn off the hinges. Both Lutzes see eyes in a window and run outside to find hoof prints in the snow. And a creepy secret room painted completely in red suddenly reeks of human feces. And these are just a few of the things that continue to happen. At one point George wakes up to find Kathleen levitating off the bed. And still they stay. For 28 days.<br /><br />If the things that George and Kathleen Lutz claim happened to them at 112 Ocean Avenue really did happen, then I can't imagine any sane person who would stay in that house for 28 days. I get that the family was strapped for cash. I understand that George was having issues with his business and the IRS, but come on. If you believe that an entity or a demon is tormenting you in your home, and they did, because they repeatedly tried to get help from a priest, I have trouble believing that anyone would stay in that environment. <br /><br />Like I said though, I'm a skeptic, and I always look for the holes in a story like this. I said I was disappointed that I bothered to finish this one, but maybe it's a good thing that I did. It's a good concept, I just don't believe that it actually happened the way the Lutzes claim it did. And I'm no longer creeped out by Jodie the pig. So bad writing and ridiculous circumstances aside, I'm glad I was finally able to put this story to rest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3041285939282409824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27865935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2161306962066961251">A family, who I shall call the Lootz family (for the sake of their privacy), moves into a house in Amityville, Long Island, where the terrible murders of the previous owners took place. Some twenty-eight days later the Lutz – er, Lootz, family flees in terror. Horrific things happened there. Blood dripped from walls; people floated about in mid air over their beds, there were flies everywhere. Worst of all, a marching band paraded through their living room at three a.m. All these horrors were or</span>
  <span id="freeText2161306962066961251" style="display:none">A family, who I shall call the Lootz family (for the sake of their privacy), moves into a house in Amityville, Long Island, where the terrible murders of the previous owners took place. Some twenty-eight days later the Lutz – er, Lootz, family flees in terror. Horrific things happened there. Blood dripped from walls; people floated about in mid air over their beds, there were flies everywhere. Worst of all, a marching band paraded through their living room at three a.m. All these horrors were orchestrated by a pig demon named Josie (name changed to protect the pig demon’s identity). <br /><br />In order to calm their nerves and find some closure, the family set down their true story with the help of a journalist friend. This book became a major bestseller and was turned into a popular movie starring Margot Kidder. Other Amityville Horror movies, albeit fictional, followed in a sort of Amityville feeding frenzy (do remember that the setting for “Jaws”, Amity, was based on Amityville), and the original was even remade with Melissa George playing Margot Kidder, er, Mrs. Lootz. There is probably tons of other tie-in merchandise spawned from the book that I’m not aware of. Amityville House Coffee Mugs (“Good to the very last drop … of blood”), for example. Or Jody the Pig Demon rocking chairs – oops, I mean Josie the Pig Demon rocking chairs. There must have been beach towels and beach balls, floating action figures, and T-shirts, too. I’m sure someone marketed Amityville Horror Fly Swatters and Li’l Ghoulie Marching Band toys. <br /><br />As a postscript: the family moved far, far away from Amityville to Arizona where, they said, the demons and ghosts followed and haunted them. Sad to say, though, the supernatural entities lost lots of their powers in the move. There was no book to bear witness to the burden these people bore, so subsequently no movies or merchandise. Josie couldn’t even get the cost of the new home returned. The poor Lootz family had to muddle through with just the licensing and residual fees off the back of the first book. <br /></span>
